# GCC Optimization Pass Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how GCC's optimization passes are registered and executed during compilation. Find all C/C++ source files in `gcc-mirror/gcc` that: 1. Define the pass execution order (`gcc/passes.def` — the master list of all passes). 2. Implement the pass manager that orchestrates pass execution (`gcc/passes.cc`). 3. Define the `opt_pass` base class and pass manager interface (`gcc/pass_manager.h`). 4. Implement a concrete GIMPLE optimization pass — specifically dead code elimination (`gcc/tree-ssa-dce.cc`). 5. Define the tree-SSA pass header (`gcc/tree-pass.h`) that declares pass registration macros. Report the repo, file path, and key struct/function name for each file.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Summary

I've documented the complete optimization pass system in GCC from the specified pinned mirror (`github.com/sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333`):

### Key Files Found:
1. **gcc/passes.def** - Master list defining pass execution order using NEXT_PASS macros
2. **gcc/passes.cc** - Implements the pass manager with `execute_one_pass()` and `execute_pass_list()` functions
3. **gcc/pass_manager.h** - Defines the `opt_pass` base class and `pass_manager` that orchestrates execution
4. **gcc/tree-pass.h** - Defines pass registration infrastructure: `pass_data` struct, `gimple_opt_pass` class, `register_pass_info` struct, and pass factory declarations
5. **gcc/tree-ssa-dce.cc** - Implements a concrete GIMPLE pass for dead code elimination with `pass_dce` class and `make_pass_dce()` factory function

### Key Symbols:
- `opt_pass` (base class with virtual `gate()` and `execute()` methods)
- `pass_manager` (manages pass pipelines)
- `pass_data` (metadata structure)
- `pass_dce` (concrete DCE pass implementation)
- `execute_one_pass()`, `execute_pass_list()` (execution chain functions)

The document includes line numbers, detailed struct/class descriptions, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how passes flow from definition through registration to execution.

{\n122:   }\n123: };\n124: \n125: /* Description of RTL pass.  */\n126: class rtl_opt_pass : public opt_pass\n127: {\n128: protected:\n129:   rtl_opt_pass (const pass_data& data, gcc::context When updating real names,\n249:    only insert PHI nodes for a real name O_j in blocks reached by all\n250:    the new and old definitions for O_j.  If the iterated dominance\n251:    frontier for O_j is not pruned, we may end up inserting PHI nodes\n252:    in blocks that have one or more edges with no incoming definition\n253:    for O_j.  This would lead to uninitialized warnings for O_j's\n254:    symbol.  */\n255: #define TODO_update_ssa\t\t\t(1 << 11)\n256: \n257: /* Update the SSA form without inserting any new PHI nodes at all.\n258:    This is used by passes that have either inserted all the PHI nodes\n259:    themselves or passes that need only to patch use-def and def-def\n260:    chains for virtuals (e.g., DCE).  */\n261: #define TODO_update_ssa_no_phi\t\t(1 << 12)\n262: \n263: /* Insert PHI nodes everywhere they are needed.  No pruning of the\n264:    IDF is done.  This is used by passes that need the PHI nodes for\n265:    O_j even if it means that some arguments will come from the default\n266:    definition of O_j's symbol.\n267: \n268:    WARNING: If you need to use this flag, chances are that your pass\n269:    may be doing something wrong.  Inserting PHI nodes for an old name\n270:    where not all edges carry a new replacement may lead to silent\n271:    codegen errors or spurious uninitialized warnings.  */\n272: #define TODO_update_ssa_full_phi\t(1 << 13)\n273: \n274: /* Passes that update the SSA form on their own may want to delegate\n275:    the updating of virtual names to the generic updater.  Since FUD\n276:    chains are easier to maintain, this simplifies the work they need\n277:    to do.  NOTE: If this flag is used, any OLD->NEW mappings for real\n278:    names are explicitly destroyed and only the symbols marked for\n279:    renaming are processed.  */\n280: #define TODO_update_ssa_only_virtuals\t(1 << 14)\n281: \n282: /* Some passes leave unused local variables that can be removed from\n283:    cfun->local_decls.  This reduces the size of dump files\n284:    and the memory footprint for VAR_DECLs.  */\n285: #define TODO_remove_unused_locals\t(1 << 15)\n286: \n287: /* Call df_finish at the end of the pass.
